<div id="review_244498833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244498833" />
    <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews"><img alt="YA Reads Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285429046p2/1764232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244498833?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YA Reads Book Reviews" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews">YA Reads Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews?shelf=kiona">kiona</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244498833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer653479699784585837">Ten Things We Did looks and sounds like a light-hearted, fun, easy read. It promises to appeal to fans of authors like Susane Colasanti, Sarah Dessen, and Lauren Myracle. But Sarah Mlynowski doesn’t quite deliver on that promise. Ten Things is a light, fun read, but the plot and characters are unrealistic. When April’s dad decides to move to Cleveland, she opts to move in with her friend Vi rather than uproot herself. Only thing is, April’s dad would freak if he found out Vi’s mom won’t be stayi</span>
  <span id="freeText653479699784585837" style="display:none">Ten Things We Did looks and sounds like a light-hearted, fun, easy read. It promises to appeal to fans of authors like Susane Colasanti, Sarah Dessen, and Lauren Myracle. But Sarah Mlynowski doesn’t quite deliver on that promise. Ten Things is a light, fun read, but the plot and characters are unrealistic. When April’s dad decides to move to Cleveland, she opts to move in with her friend Vi rather than uproot herself. Only thing is, April’s dad would freak if he found out Vi’s mom won’t be staying with them, leaving the two teenagers alone in Vi’s spacious home. To placate April’s dad, the girls provide him with a fake email address and Vi dutifully responds to all his emails as if she were her mom.<br /><br />As if this scenario weren’t crazy enough, the ridiculous situations the girls continuously get themselves into drive this story over the top. While it tries to be charming and endearing, it’s hard to forget just how improbable all of it is. As a main character, April is kind of forgettable. Vi is much more interesting, but she’s also the proponent of this whole scheme and I kind of hold that against her. My favorite characters are brothers Dean and Hudson, but they don’t appear enough to really satisfy me.<br /><br />I will say Ten Things explores some real teen issues and deals with them in a relatable, believable way, specifically issues surrounding relationships, sex, infidelity, conforming, and friendship. Some conversations are reminiscent of conversations every girl has had with or can imagining have with a friend. And if you can suspend your disbelief for a little while, the craziness that is April’s life can even be funny. You’ll wistfully imagine your own life parent- and rule-free for a few minutes. Then you’ll get to the end and realize you don’t want to have the conversation that April’s about to have with her dad.<br /><br />If you’re looking for a light, quick read, then Ten Things We Did (And Probably Shouldn’t Have) will probably satisfy you. If you want something with a little more substance, I’d suggest you keep looking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="653479699784585837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1416517796" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416517796" />
    <a title="Tijana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45530304-tijana"><img alt="Tijana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440200000p2/45530304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416517796?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tijana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tijana" href="/user/show/45530304-tijana">Tijana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416517796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14913452194727327387">3.5 stars (close to 4?)<br/><br/>I'm currently in a phase of reading teenage books. <br/>I guess I realized that, in a couple of years, I'll completely outgrow them and I'll have the rest of my life for reading the serious adult ones, so why would I do that now? <br/><br/>Anyhow...<br/>Sarah Mlynowski is a good writer. About 10 years ago, I was crazy about the Magic in Manhattan series, so I thought I might give a try to other books written by this author, too. <br/>I don't regret it.<br/>Ten Things We Did is one of the most original </span>
  <span id="freeText14913452194727327387" style="display:none">3.5 stars (close to 4?)<br /><br />I'm currently in a phase of reading teenage books. <br />I guess I realized that, in a couple of years, I'll completely outgrow them and I'll have the rest of my life for reading the serious adult ones, so why would I do that now? <br /><br />Anyhow...<br />Sarah Mlynowski is a good writer. About 10 years ago, I was crazy about the Magic in Manhattan series, so I thought I might give a try to other books written by this author, too. <br />I don't regret it.<br />Ten Things We Did is one of the most original teen books I've read when it comes to the plot, diversity of characters is amazing and the most important thing: they all were really 16-17 y/o.<br />It happens often for a writer to make a story about teenagers, but somehow ends up making them seem like they're in their mid 20's.<br />Here it's not a case.<br />They were all adorably clueless, their emotions were raw, actions crazy, drinking hard and relationships taken way to seriously for kids that are still in high school. But I loved it! Reminded me a lot of my wild 16 year old self and can't deny I laught out loud at cartain points.<br /><br />Very (bitter)sweet!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14913452194727327387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1798936550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1798936550" />
    <a title="Glire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7227066-glire"><img alt="Glire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572949569p2/7227066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1798936550?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glire" href="/user/show/7227066-glire">Glire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10474408-ten-things-we-did">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7227066-glire?shelf=clich%C3%A9ratura">clichératura</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7227066-glire?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798936550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2546986326780852461">Me ha encantado la manera en que está escrito este libro: la narrativa es relajada, divertida y ligeramente irónica.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote><b>THREE MONTHS EARLIER</b><br/>“How would you like to finish high school in Cleveland?” my dad asked me out of nowhere during Christmas break of junior year.<br/>Fine. Maybe it wasn’t completely out of nowhere.<br/><br/><b>THREE MONTHS, ONE MINUTE, THIRTY SECONDS EARLIER</b><br/>“April, can you sit down? We need to talk to you about an important issue.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>La trama no es sumamente original pero está bien desarrollada</b>, </span>
  <span id="freeText2546986326780852461" style="display:none">Me ha encantado la manera en que está escrito este libro: la narrativa es relajada, divertida y ligeramente irónica.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote><b>THREE MONTHS EARLIER</b><br />“How would you like to finish high school in Cleveland?” my dad asked me out of nowhere during Christmas break of junior year.<br />Fine. Maybe it wasn’t completely out of nowhere.<br /><br /><b>THREE MONTHS, ONE MINUTE, THIRTY SECONDS EARLIER</b><br />“April, can you sit down? We need to talk to you about an important issue.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>La trama no es sumamente original pero está bien desarrollada</b>, entremezclando entretenimiento puro con temas más serios (el abandono familiar, el perdón y la confianza son pilares fundamentales de la historia). Además, <b>se lee rapidísimo</b>. ¿Lo malo? El final. Es apresurado y, honestamente, me ha sabido a poco. Aún así, el libro cumple con su objetivo: <b>entretener sin mayores pretensiones.</b> Y fácil fácil puedo verlo convertido en una película, resultaría mejor que la de <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931356.The_DUFF_Designated_Ugly_Fat_Friend" title="The DUFF Designated Ugly Fat Friend by Kody Keplinger" rel="nofollow noopener">The DUFF: Designated Ugly Fat Friend</a>, eso es indudable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2546986326780852461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159498988?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159498988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3872337034941260280">Pretty much the entire plot of this book revolves around sex. Oh, and lying to your parents in a major way for an extended period of time. Add a lot of heavy drinking and partying into the mix, and that's this book.<br/><br/>The circumstances and the behavior of the adults and teens are just too unbelievable. I felt like I was reading about a wild sorority house in college instead of a bunch of 16-year-olds. (Yeah, I'm supposed to believe these high schoolers fool their parents into letting them live alon</span>
  <span id="freeText3872337034941260280" style="display:none">Pretty much the entire plot of this book revolves around sex. Oh, and lying to your parents in a major way for an extended period of time. Add a lot of heavy drinking and partying into the mix, and that's this book.<br /><br />The circumstances and the behavior of the adults and teens are just too unbelievable. I felt like I was reading about a wild sorority house in college instead of a bunch of 16-year-olds. (Yeah, I'm supposed to believe these high schoolers fool their parents into letting them live alone without adult supervision and daddy bankrolls it by giving our protag $1000 a month...and when our protag confesses to her mom, her mom doesn't care because she's too petty to talk to her ex-husband???)<br /><br />And I'm sorry, but kids who skip school and get drunk on school nights and don't study do not get full rides into Columbia and NYU. Can we please be a little realistic here?<br /><br />There's a lot more to teens than sex and getting drunk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3872337034941260280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GUBue20xNzlkDvC75+OdYOyBxXvLSMYpqo/L+EA+sdsu7AXYNOtoPZ2s9YJiOHSTjAgu0Bppx8QRYFJ0PmKeTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SanM50usbWHn15sP6T85aRBpwfcFrnkZorCG6tTfq7d+BadEEnYyZR51njZs5NCacOAqXNSPePQZXx9mqoOEIg==')})
  }

But he\'s never seemed to notice that Reena even exists until one day, impossibly, he does. Reena and Sawyer fall in messy, complicated love. But then Sawyer disappears from their humid Florida town without a word, leaving a devastated—and pregnant—Reena behind. \n\n\n  After:\n\nAlmost three years have passed, and there\'s a new love in Reena\'s life: her daughter, Hannah. Reena\'s gotten used to being without Sawyer, and she\'s finally getting the hang of this strange, unexpected life. But just as swiftly and suddenly as he disappeared, Sawyer turns up again. Reena doesn\'t want anything to do with him, though she\'d be lying if she said Sawyer\'s being back wasn\'t stirring something in her. After everything that\'s happened, can Reena really let herself love Sawyer LeGrande again?\n\nIn this breathtaking debut, Katie Cotugno weaves together the story of one couple falling in love—twice.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7422191424890900082\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/771.Sarah_Mlynowski">About Sarah Mlynowski</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/771.Sarah_Mlynowski"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1209389266p3/771.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/771.Sarah_Mlynowski">Sarah Mlynowski

<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15068951855401301306">Sarah was born in Montreal, Canada. After graduating with an honors degree in English literature from McGill University, she moved to Toronto to work for Harlequin Enterprises. While she never met Fabio, she used her romance publishing experiences to fuel her first novel Milkrun. <br/><br/>Since then, Sarah has written ﻿four additional novels for adults: Fishbowl, As Seen on TV, Monkey Business, and Me vs. </span>
  <span id="freeText15068951855401301306" style="display:none">Sarah was born in Montreal, Canada. After graduating with an honors degree in English literature from McGill University, she moved to Toronto to work for Harlequin Enterprises. While she never met Fabio, she used her romance publishing experiences to fuel her first novel Milkrun. <br /><br />Since then, Sarah has written ﻿four additional novels for adults: Fishbowl, As Seen on TV, Monkey Business, and Me vs. Me; the New York Times bestselling middle grade series Whatever After; the middle grade series Upside-Down Magic (with Lauren Myracle and Emily Jenkins); and the teen novels Bras &amp; Broomsticks, Frogs &amp; French Kisses, Spells &amp; Sleeping Bags, and Parties &amp; Potions (all in the Magic in Manhattan series), as well as Gimme a Call, Ten Things We Did (And Probably Shouldn't Have), Don't Even Think About It, Think Twice, and I See London, I See France. Along with Lauren Myracle and E. Lockhart, Sarah also wrote How to Be Bad, and along with Farrin Jacobs, she wrote See Jane Write, a guide to writing. Sarah also co-edited two bestselling charity collections (Girls' Night In and Girls' Night Out), and has contributed to various anthologies (American Girls About Town, Sixteen: Stories About That Sweet and Bitter Birthday, 21 Proms, First Kiss (Then Tell), Fireworks, and Vacations from Hell). <br /><br />Sarah is also a co-founder of OMG BookFest, a celebration of books aimed at the early to middle grade reader (ages 7-12) that brings together commercial and award-winning authors with underserved local communities for an exciting experience of books, games and activities.<br /><br />Sarah's books have been translated into twenty-nine languages and optioned to Hollywood. She now lives in New York City with her husband and two daughters.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15068951855401301306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
